  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_03773dce-f44e-42f2-b715-62d65d90fd2b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1676437693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1676437693" />
    <a title="Chelsea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea"><img alt="Chelsea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537582300p2/33012180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1676437693?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea" href="/user/show/33012180-chelsea">Chelsea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545685405" href="/book/show/30254963-talons-of-power">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012180-chelsea?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676437693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4200938572639603974">My final book of 2016! <b>I thoroughly enjoyed the reading experience of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29550388.Talons_of_Power__Wings_of_Fire___9_' title='Talons of Power (Wings of Fire, #9) by Tui T. Sutherland' rel='nofollow noopener'>Talons of Power</a>, never finding myself uninterested. That being said, I think this is definitely the weakest book in the second arc and most of the book can be classified as filler.</b> 3 ½ stars<br/><br/>Before I get into my issues, let me preface this by saying I adore the Wings of Fire books and consider this one of my all time favorite middle grade series. My critiques of this book do not change that, and 3 ½ stars is a positive rating f</span>
  <span id="freeText4200938572639603974" style="display:none">My final book of 2016! <b>I thoroughly enjoyed the reading experience of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29550388.Talons_of_Power__Wings_of_Fire___9_" title="Talons of Power (Wings of Fire, #9) by Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Talons of Power</a>, never finding myself uninterested. That being said, I think this is definitely the weakest book in the second arc and most of the book can be classified as filler.</b> 3 ½ stars<br /><br />Before I get into my issues, let me preface this by saying I adore the Wings of Fire books and consider this one of my all time favorite middle grade series. My critiques of this book do not change that, and 3 ½ stars is a positive rating for me.<br /><br /><b>Other than the last 20 pages or so, this book is the same thing happening over and over again.</b> Turtle follows Darkstalker, waiting for him to do something evil, Darkstalker doesn’t. Repeat for 200 pages.<br /><br />Turtle is a very…passive character. He spends nearly the entire book “invisible” and just hanging out observing everyone else. He rarely takes matters into his own hands, which I recognize is part of his character but it makes him so much less interesting compared to the other main characters like Moon or Peril.<br /><br /><b>Turtle is so infrequently involved in the story that he didn’t even feel like the main character.</b> Most of this book is slow and repetitive. A lot of the plot serves to bridge the gap to the series finale.<br /><br />Though I was let down by this penultimate novel, I still enjoyed reading it. I love this series and world. <b>The characters of this arc are extremely endearing. I’ve been reading Tui’s writing since I was very young, so I’m always happy to jump into her stories.</b><br /><br />I’m still super hyped for the finale (which I hope is the actual finale; this series does not need another extension). <b>There are so many ways this could go, and I can’t wait to see.</b> Not to mention I think Qibli is the main character of the final book, and he is one of my favorites!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4200938572639603974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2623171666" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2623171666" />
    <a title="LeafOreo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89272719-leaforeo"><img alt="LeafOreo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577282982p2/89272719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2623171666?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LeafOreo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LeafOreo" href="/user/show/89272719-leaforeo">LeafOreo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30688973-talons-of-power">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89272719-leaforeo?shelf=favourite-books-of-all-time">favourite-books-of-all-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/89272719-leaforeo?shelf=wings-of-fire">wings-of-fire</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2623171666" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2382921940998218714">I actually finished this book a while ago but forgot to update my progress.<br/><br/>I'll review it now, but make it brief.<br/><br/>*spoilers*<br/><br/>The book really made me wonder about the truth of the relationship of animus magic to a dragon's soul. Does using animus magic really make one's soul deteriorate? Only if the intention is bad? If one is using their animus magic for a good intention, does that not deteriorate their soul as much? Well, I certainly believe now that the magic does have a negative impact on the s</span>
  <span id="freeText2382921940998218714" style="display:none">I actually finished this book a while ago but forgot to update my progress.<br /><br />I'll review it now, but make it brief.<br /><br />*spoilers*<br /><br />The book really made me wonder about the truth of the relationship of animus magic to a dragon's soul. Does using animus magic really make one's soul deteriorate? Only if the intention is bad? If one is using their animus magic for a good intention, does that not deteriorate their soul as much? Well, I certainly believe now that the magic does have a negative impact on the soul - but not always. If it's used for a good intention, then it does not. Which makes sense, because it wouldn't be logical for a dragon full of goodness just abruptly turning evil (losing their soul). <br /><br />Anyway. Moving on.<br /><br />I loved this book since it was from Turtle's (the humble son of Queen Coral) point of view. How he hides his magic, how he feels about being an animus, what he has enchanted so far with his gift and a secret about Anemone. Oh, and yeah, his feelings about Kinkajou, which I thought was adorable. &lt;3<br /><br />Okay, I'll just say it, since I already warned y'all of spoilers above.<br /><br />Turtle gave Anemone her animus powers, to hide his own.<br /><br />This book follows the dramatic scene where Peril burns Darkstalker's scroll and sends all his magic back to him, so that he could use it to escape his underground mountain prison that had him imprisoned for over 2000 years. The reason why there is such a massive cliffhanger between the previous book and this one is because Darkstalker finally gets freed, and you never know what he will do...<br /><br />Until you read this book.<br /><br />In the end, there's an epic battle between two animus siblings: Turtle and his sister Anemone.<br /><br />And they both get kidnapped by Darkstalker, who (UGHGHGHHHH!) takes Turtle's animus powers away.<br /><br />Turtle, on the whole, was an interesting character. From book 6, he was pretty shady overall and you don't get to see inside his head because of his skyfire, so Moon can't read him.<br /><br />His design is amazing, too. Love how he has green scales like his father and blue bioluminescent stripes like Coral. Beautiful indeed.<br /><br />Just wanna give Turtle a big hug. He's deserving of that..<br /><br /><br /><br />All right, that was not brief.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2382921940998218714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1852070814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1852070814" />
    <a title="Lightwavers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63070028-lightwavers"><img alt="Lightwavers" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1852070814?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lightwavers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lightwavers" href="/user/show/63070028-lightwavers">Lightwavers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63070028-lightwavers?shelf=cliff-hangar">cliff-hangar</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852070814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17910438694949184708">Finally, the ninth book is out! Woohoo!<br/><br/>If you're wondering if you should read this: a huge YES, bearing in mind that it is the ninth book of the series, but beware it's just as much a cliffhanger as the last one.<br/><br/>WARNING: SPOILERS BELOW<br/><br/>The book starts out right after the last one. Pearl unwittingly freed Darkstalker after she burned his scroll of power, and now all his powers have flowed right back into him. Right after he's freed, Turtle enchants a stick to hide him from Darkstalker, because Tur</span>
  <span id="freeText17910438694949184708" style="display:none">Finally, the ninth book is out! Woohoo!<br /><br />If you're wondering if you should read this: a huge YES, bearing in mind that it is the ninth book of the series, but beware it's just as much a cliffhanger as the last one.<br /><br />WARNING: SPOILERS BELOW<br /><br />The book starts out right after the last one. Pearl unwittingly freed Darkstalker after she burned his scroll of power, and now all his powers have flowed right back into him. Right after he's freed, Turtle enchants a stick to hide him from Darkstalker, because Turtle can smell evil intentions a mile away.<br /><br />So now we have an invisible Turtle and a freed Darkstaker. Now that he's freed, he doesn't want a repeat of last time (read Darkstalker Legends if you haven't already) so he decides to enchant everyone he meets to be friends with him. We get a bit of Darkstalker's 2,000 year old hugeness inhabiting Jade Mountain and giving the Nightwings there trinkets that grant powers (such as mind reading and super strength) which are referred to as the 'Talons of Power'. He spends some time magnanimously forgiving everyone who attacks him and acting like a saint while Turtle watches, as well as acting the tiniest bit evil to put us on edge. Oh, and he gets Anenome on his side too, and since they both have soul protectors, the spells are a-flyin'. (Psssst, Anenome's bracers control the weather. How cool is that? Of course, we only see them once in the entire book, grumble grumble.)<br /><br />Then Darkstalker decides he still wants his kingdom, so he travels over to Gory's part of town, enchanting everyone he meets. Now the Nightwings there are actually having a pretty neat time of things, so Darkstalker postpones his "join me underlings!" speech in favour of making everyone like him. Of course, the passive "everyone must adore me" spell is going on in the background, but Darkstalker goes above and beyond by giving away more 'Talons of Power', while we get some quality Turtle Time. Darkstalker can sense animus uses now, so Turtle pretends to be a lil weakling and asks the Great Anenome to heal Kinkajou. Anenome heals her, but also puts a love spell on her. Now we've got the setup for a "spell gets broken, turns out she really loved him all along moment". But I digress. So Darkstalker's mass charming everyone. If I were Darkstalker, I'd think a bit (REMEMBER CLEARSIGHT?!) and try being honest for once, but noooooo. Ahem.<br /><br />So Darkstalker gets his adoring fans—I mean, kingdom of Nightwings—and goes soaring off into the sunset. Turtle, Moon, and Kinkajou fly after to prevent evil horribad things that will happen because Sutherland just couldn't let Darkstalker be a good guy. LIKE SERIOUSLY, WHY. I WAS LIKE CRYING ONCE I UNDERSTOOD THE PLOT. At least let him be a "oh I'm sorry I understand I was a bad boy I'll be good now" character after he's inevitably defeated in the next book.<br /><br />The Nightwings reach the ancient kingdom of the night soon enough, and Anenome turns naughty and knocks poor Moon about because she's jelly over Darkstalker's mooning over Moon. So Darkstalker flies into a rage and banishes Anenome to the sea kingdom, telling her to go kill anyone who gets in her way. Because reasons. Now Turtle gets scared (And yes, I know scared's his default state. I mean scarder) and races after Anenome. Then we find out that, OH MY, Turtle was the one who gave Anenome her powers in the first place, because he wanted to not be noticed. Then Turtle finishes his flashback and actually finds Anenome. The odds look to be in his favour, because he finds her right before she's about to enchant a knife to kill her family. Awesome right? Well, if you like the royal Seawing family. I think it's about getting the readers to think NOOOO, BABY AUKLET, but anyway.<br /><br />So we have an epic animus battle between Anenome and Turtle, where he accidentally turns himself invincible forever (but not immortal) and actually wins without killing Anenome, because of Plot Armour. And somehow he turns her into a good guy. Yay? I bet she'll never have to own up to beating Moon about with a mop. And also we get told that souls don't matter, it's pretty much just a "power corrupts" type thing.<br /><br />But, OH NO, Darkstalker senses the huge animus battle going on, but only conveniently after the fight's finished, of course. He summons all the animus dragons in the world to his throne room, including an unknown Sandwing who teleports away in a split second before he even notices. Only THEN does he put a spell preventing other animus dragons in the room from using their power. Honestly, his brains must've partially frozen during his sleep. He could've done that BEFORE summoning everyone there, or even extended the spell to stop every other dragon from using animus powers, REGARDLESS of their location. Ugh. Moving on, he is smart enough to realise Turtle's there and Anenome wasn't just having a tantrum, but instead of saying "Make all spells from an animus dragon other than me stop working," he just brings in "a dragon important to the animus hiding in the room." I ask you...<br /><br />Still, Darkstalker's incompetence is (somehow) greatly exceeded by the incompetence of every other dragon in the world, and he does reveal and then remember Turtle... but was too stupid to remove spells other than his in the throne room, so Turtle throws his invisibility stick to Anenome, who escapes. Through a window.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Darkstalker goes all muahahaha, gotcha, but I would never really harm Kinkajou cause she's Moon's friend. Then he says the same of Turtle. After trying to burn him to death because Fathom, but invincibility spell. And then says his resemblance to Fathom is causing him to want to murder him, so Turtle's gotta go into the dungeons. And on the way Darkstalker zaps Turtle's animus power. So that's a bummer, Turtle's normal now. Sheesh, animus dragons can do anything, can't they. Makes me long for the sensible magic of Brandon Sanderson books...<br /><br />But hey! At least Turtle's still invincible, right? Because Darkstalker wouldn't even THINK of removing animus enchants from a former animus. So we've got to wait for Anenome to inevitably save the day.<br /><br />BUT WAIT!!!! Before you go. Let's show some scenes from around the world! So... Uh... Sand Kindom, we've got terrorist dragons with black hoods (yeah, I don't know how they'd wear 'em either) and golden bird medallions blowing things up. Over in the Sea Kingdom, we've got the ghost of Albatross haunting people(?!?!?!), and in the Ice Kingdom everyone's caught a disease and is dying horribly. Queen's already dead too.<br /><br />So. Loved the book, but yet ANOTHER cliff-hangar makes me mad, so 4 stars for you. Also, while character stupidity continues to irritate me, it IS a children's book, so I'm letting it slide. ;)<br /><br />You can read this review on my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://xilandre.wordpress.com">https://xilandre.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17910438694949184708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1748294644?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amariah Dixon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amariah Dixon" href="/user/show/19327882-amariah-dixon">Amariah Dixon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1748294644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12310879908631128562">I read in an interview by the author last summer that this one was going to be the book in the series where the story "rips your heart out and stomps on it". I didn't really find that in here, but the ending is a major cliff-hanger! Darkstalker has definitely gotten on my nerves, even though he does have a sad background for why he does what he does. <br/><br/>Turtle, every once in a while, annoyed me with his "maybe someone else will save the world while I go hide safely in a corner!" bit. Okay, so he's </span>
  <span id="freeText12310879908631128562" style="display:none">I read in an interview by the author last summer that this one was going to be the book in the series where the story "rips your heart out and stomps on it". I didn't really find that in here, but the ending is a major cliff-hanger! Darkstalker has definitely gotten on my nerves, even though he does have a sad background for why he does what he does. <br /><br />Turtle, every once in a while, annoyed me with his "maybe someone else will save the world while I go hide safely in a corner!" bit. Okay, so he's terrified of Darkstalker discovering his powers, but his reactions sort of irked me. <br /><br />On the other hand, I was drawn in to this story from the first page! I did feel sorry for Turtle, though. He was teased and criticized when he was younger. There is no doubt that I found this to be thoroughly engaging and the characters feel very real! I love the detail, and the suspense keeps you on the edge of your seat. <br />I cannot wait to read the last book!</span>

          </span>

        <a title="Trixi #WATERFLAME" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trixi #WATERFLAME" href="/user/show/45203704-trixi-waterflame">Trixi #WATERFLAME</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Preteens who don't mind book violence</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1896747849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6185971878772582845">I feel like nothing big was resolved in this book other than some events Tui planned to happen.<br/>So before I start my review, I'll just say I'm not expecting very much of Book 10.<br/>NOT because this book sucked (part 1 was boring, though)<br/>NOT because it's from Qibli's point of view (it's bound to be interesting)<br/>BUT it's because of the very abrupt way Tui ends her book series.<br/>The Brightest Night was a very abrupt ending in which Tui got rid of two sisters hurriedly in one chapter (they've lived for 20 </span>
  <span id="freeText6185971878772582845" style="display:none">I feel like nothing big was resolved in this book other than some events Tui planned to happen.<br />So before I start my review, I'll just say I'm not expecting very much of Book 10.<br />NOT because this book sucked (part 1 was boring, though)<br />NOT because it's from Qibli's point of view (it's bound to be interesting)<br />BUT it's because of the very abrupt way Tui ends her book series.<br />The Brightest Night was a very abrupt ending in which Tui got rid of two sisters hurriedly in one chapter (they've lived for 20 years of war! Their abrupt deaths are just so forced.) <br />And Tui's got a LOT of things to resolve in just one book, which means defeating Onyx, Darkstalker and crowning the new IceWing queen.<br />It's an amazing series but things are always resolved at the last minute!<br /><br />So, Turtle.<br />("......the most boring prince on the planet." -Anemone)<br />It is actually half true since he was following Darkstalker around invisibly for the whole part 1. Continue for half of part 2.<br />Kinkajou is back and I'm so happy about that. I ship her with Turtle but then I realised the ship is quite similar to Starflight and Sunny(timid male dragon likes cheerful female dragon)<br />I hope Turtle and Kinkajou will happen, though.<br />Then we have the epic animus battle, Turtle is finally revealed, he loses his animus power (and I hate that part). <br />Now I have heard that some people ship Moon with DARKSTALKER.<br />Darkstalker is creepy and honestly I don't think he deserves Moon because he is just plain evil and he shows absolutely no sign of remorse for his actions. So no offense but I think Moon is happier and better off with Winter or Qibli (personally I ship Moon with Winter)<br />Characters are well-developed<br />I liked Anemone in book 2, she was so adorable back then and I was very disappointed to find that she is now a spoiled, bratty princess.<br />Kinkajou is my favourite character and I hope there will be a Winglets for her at least about her detailed experience in the Night Kingdom, how she persevered from the torture of being imprisoned and experimented on in such a horrible place.<br />Review Conclusion: actually my least favourite book in the second arc, though better than books 4 and 5.</span>

Should we beware of hailstorm?)<br /><br />Something is coming to shake the earth(yahooi, Darkstalker has risen...)<br />Something is coming to scorch the ground(no seriously, major wild fires?)<br />Jade Mountain will fall beneath thunder and ice(still same old hypothesis. Icewings and ....Thunderclan will dramatically battle out everything. I guess Thunder is Nightwings. Or it will just be randomly snowing that night)<br />Unless the lost city of night can be found( BUT ITS ALREADY BEEN FOUND HUH anyways I was always like "major secrets will be uncovered here TAHT will explain everything yay")</span>

  <span id="freeText8711423630830077316" style="display:none">*warning-this text contains spoilers*<br />I loved this book soooooo much! It was very interesting to see Turtle’s POV, as well as Darkstalker.<br />Now, about him...<br />Doesn’t Darkstalker remind you a little bit of Donald Trump?<br />He came to the Rain Kingdom to challenge Glory for the throne, and most of the resident NightWings were hesitant about this, because of him being this TWO-THOUSAND YEAR OLD EVIL FREAK DUDE, but as soon as he started using his powers on them (and doling out superpowers to them...”You get a superpower! You get a superpower! EVERYONE gets a superpower!!!”), they immediately like him and most go with him to rebuild the Night Kingdom-MAKING THE NIGHTWINGS GREAT AGAIN. <br />I don’t think this was intended, but this book actually makes a bit of a social commentary, which I enjoyed. Very interesting. And so, I made this: <br />/Users/Madeline/Desktop/Darkstalker is literally Trump.jpg<br />Anyway, another amazing WOF installment. I look forward to book 10!<br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3613807061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4528086857233515367">So I get why people might have a harder time with this one, since Turtle is a little more passive than the other dragons and a little more timid. But I'm writing this one after I just finished book ten (I'm a little behind) and I think I understand now why he's written this way. I did not find this one boring at all, but he was definitely a hide and think and watch kind of character. And I think it really comes into play with how things resolve in book #10. I'm not gonna give anything away, but </span>
  <span id="freeText4528086857233515367" style="display:none">So I get why people might have a harder time with this one, since Turtle is a little more passive than the other dragons and a little more timid. But I'm writing this one after I just finished book ten (I'm a little behind) and I think I understand now why he's written this way. I did not find this one boring at all, but he was definitely a hide and think and watch kind of character. And I think it really comes into play with how things resolve in book #10. I'm not gonna give anything away, but if you're a fan of the series, be patient. Turtle might be quiet and not impulsively exciting like some other characters, but he has definite worth. And there are some gems of scenes in this book that tickled me pink. I try not to expect anything out of these characters, and in doing so, am always pleasantly surprised by the plot twists. Not my favorite out of the series, but still worth the read.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1862644054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1862644054" />
    <a title="Denae Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/857888-denae-christine"><img alt="Denae Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446784625p2/857888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1862644054?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denae Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denae Christine" href="/user/show/857888-denae-christine">Denae Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1862644054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer75406509094363780"><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I wasn't sure I'd like reading about an animus dragon (Turtle), because he's too powerful. Indeed, the animus power does need more limitations. Darkstalker and Anemone throw around spells as fast as a greeting. However, Turtle doesn't use his animus power flippantly. He's careful and timid. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[And I hate that Darkstalker took his power away at the end! <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>This book might be the first that doesn't show any scavengers. Oh, Turtle flies over an abandoned sca</span>
  <span id="freeText75406509094363780" style="display:none"><b>Reader thoughts:</b> I wasn't sure I'd like reading about an animus dragon (Turtle), because he's too powerful. Indeed, the animus power does need more limitations. Darkstalker and Anemone throw around spells as fast as a greeting. However, Turtle doesn't use his animus power flippantly. He's careful and timid. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I hate that Darkstalker took his power away at the end! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This book might be the first that doesn't show any scavengers. Oh, Turtle flies over an abandoned scavenger den, but he never catches/frees/scares any scavengers himself. Or maybe I missed something.<br /><br />I like reading about sneaky bad guys when you can't tell if they're really evil or not until the end. Maybe Darkstalker is just creepy. Maybe he's just controlling. Maybe it's not his fault . . . but it totally is. He's evil, and he charms/spells everyone around him into thinking they can trust him. He's like a sticky oily kind of evil. He thinks he's charming and lovable, but he's just scary underneath.<br /><br />I like how much Turtle keeps trying to save his sister, even as she turns evil. He's loyal and keeps trying to help, no matter what she does to him first.<br /><br />As much as I love the new books (6, 7, 8, and 9), the dragons in them have too much power. There seems to be too much focus on special powers (mindreading, fire scales, animus magic) rather than sheer brains. I liked that about the first few books, that the dragonets had to rely on cleverness and each other rather than special powers. I'm hoping the 10th book will be about a powerless dragon (and a little searching shows the pov character should be Qibli, whom I preferred over Kinkajou anyway).<br /><br />Normally I like special-powered characters. I'm not sure why it bothers me in this series (and the five-star ratings show it doesn't bother me much). Maybe it's that the animus power doesn't have enough limitations and overshadows the other powers too much.<br /><br /><b>Writer thoughts:</b> The prologue/backstory for Turtle felt too similar to Winter's. Both were young and made a mistake that cost them a sibling or two. They've carried around that guilt for years. It's a very nice motivation and deepens Turtle's character/personality, but we just had that two books ago! Why are all these dragons flying around and thinking they're incompetent? The "testing-day-spelling-Anemone" backstory could have been Turtle's prologue instead. It's different. And could still carry a bunch of guilt and worry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="75406509094363780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2523828624&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2523828624" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14295684403444948790">I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again. SUTHERLAND IS SUCH AN AMAZING AUTHOR! How does she constantly add books to this series that:<br/>1: Don’t seem forced<br/>2: Don’t all seem the same<br/>3: Have CRAZY verity in each character, yet the new traits in the characters don’t seem forced<br/>Each book is so different, each character is so different, and, like I said, their differences don’t seem forced. I’ve heard of book characters (not of this series) that have quirks that are forced, when these aren’t at all! </span>
  <span id="freeText14295684403444948790" style="display:none">I’ve said it before and I’ll say it again. SUTHERLAND IS SUCH AN AMAZING AUTHOR! How does she constantly add books to this series that:<br />1: Don’t seem forced<br />2: Don’t all seem the same<br />3: Have CRAZY verity in each character, yet the new traits in the characters don’t seem forced<br />Each book is so different, each character is so different, and, like I said, their differences don’t seem forced. I’ve heard of book characters (not of this series) that have quirks that are forced, when these aren’t at all! The story line is fresh in each book and so lively! There are so many plot twists and new things added to the story that keep the story alive and new and moving. <br />Also, each book being of the perspective of a different character is so awesome. You get the insight of how hat character feels about events and how they look at life, as well as seeing their fears and likes.<br />It is also so cool that in this book, we got to explode Turtle’s life as an animus! It was just as cool as exploring Moon’s mind reading or Peril’s firescales! Sutherland also explores some things people might deal with. Like social anxiety with Moon or not feeling accepted with Peril or not feeling loved or not wanting attention, with Turtle, who also almost seemed to have OCD to me. I don’t know. <br />Now about this book specifically. <br />First of all, this book seemed so... off. There wasn’t necessarily anything happening that was bad, you just KNEW something was happening and you couldn’t figure it out! It was so crazy to have Anemone go bad. She was such and innocent and lovable character in Tsunami’s book. <br />I almost felt that her atonement was a little too quick, however, Turtle’s atonements did not seem too forced. <br />But that fight scene was so epic! Two animus against each other was so awesome. <br />There was also some weird air of darkness and sadness in this book. For some reason there were parts that were just stressful! And they don’t usually give me that feeling. It was almost like the last couple Harry Potter books. I mean, nothing about that is bad, it was just weird . Because stressful things happened in the other books too. I don’t know. I think a good comparison would be the 6th Harry Potter book. It just kinda ended... off. <br />Once again, the plot twists!! Crazy. There was so much going on in the end!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14295684403444948790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1833350822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1833350822" />
    <a title="melody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/60275584-melody"><img alt="melody" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1833350822?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="melody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="melody" href="/user/show/60275584-melody">melody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545685405" href="/book/show/30254963-talons-of-power">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60275584-melody?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60275584-melody?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1833350822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5772967288842761840"><i> " Darkstalker cupped his talons around Turtle's face. 'Enchant this dragon to lose all his animus power right now," he said, "so that he shall never be able to cast a spell again." </i><br/><br/>The book was absolutely brilliant. The suspense is building and I just need to know what happens to Turtle and everybody else in the Jade Winglet. I just thought the pace of the book was a bit slow for my liking. I would have prefered for the book to have been a bit quicker. Also, the beginning of the book dragged a </span>
  <span id="freeText5772967288842761840" style="display:none"><i> " Darkstalker cupped his talons around Turtle's face. 'Enchant this dragon to lose all his animus power right now," he said, "so that he shall never be able to cast a spell again." </i><br /><br />The book was absolutely brilliant. The suspense is building and I just need to know what happens to Turtle and everybody else in the Jade Winglet. I just thought the pace of the book was a bit slow for my liking. I would have prefered for the book to have been a bit quicker. Also, the beginning of the book dragged a bit. <br />Otherwise, the book was a page-turner and I couldn't stop reading it. I love how Kinkajou is awake again. I missed her.<br /><br />Now about Darkstalker. I am speechless. This dragon . . .<br />First he just emerges out the ground and befriends all the dragons he sees, by brainwashing them all. He then travels to the Rainforest Kingdom and brainwashes Glory and Deathbringer into handing over the NightWing tribe to him. In order to convince the NightWings to choose him as king, he starts 'giving out' powers to random NightWings, like he's giving them birthday presents.<br />That's . . . just wrong.<br /><br />The thing about Darkstalker is that part of me says he's evil, but the other part says that he's changed. It's hard to decide, but only because of what he did to Turtle and all the animus dragons in the end of the book, I've decided to categorise him as 'evil.' I guess I'll have to wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33198183.Darkness_of_Dragons__Wings_of_Fire__Book_10_" title="Darkness of Dragons (Wings of Fire, Book 10) by Tui T. Sutherland" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkness of Dragons</a> in order to find out if I'm right or wrong. <br /><br />I think it's sort of cute how Darkstalker cares for Moon, but in a weird way. I can tell he really does care about her, but I'm not entirely sure why. Does Moon look a lot like Clearsight? It's adorable, but I don't ship it. (I understand some people do) Winterwatcher or Qibliwatcher are by top ships for Moon. As long as one of them sails, I'll be happy.<br /><br />I'm just really excited to read Darkness of Dragons. I hope it is a good finale for the Wings of Fire series. I hope Tui still writes more about the world of Pyrrhia.<br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2142030518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer108971291550314469">The book entitled "Wings of Fire Book 9: Talons of Power" by Tui T. Sutherland, is a thrilling, attention grabber book that makes you want to read for hours. Turtle reminds me of myself a little bit, a nice, shy, delightful person who always gets themselves into trouble. The secrets that unfold are amazing and will leave you jaw dropped, but when he gets himself into trouble he always finds a way out of it. Quibli, Kinkachiou, Moon, winter, well, maybe not him, but they are all there for him and</span>
  <span id="freeText108971291550314469" style="display:none">The book entitled "Wings of Fire Book 9: Talons of Power" by Tui T. Sutherland, is a thrilling, attention grabber book that makes you want to read for hours. Turtle reminds me of myself a little bit, a nice, shy, delightful person who always gets themselves into trouble. The secrets that unfold are amazing and will leave you jaw dropped, but when he gets himself into trouble he always finds a way out of it. Quibli, Kinkachiou, Moon, winter, well, maybe not him, but they are all there for him and to support him no matter what! This book and book series I suggest to you all because it will always have an adventure waiting for you and you will never get tired of reading it. When Turtle got chosen to spy on Darkstalker ( a dragon who was known to be a killer, an animus, mind reader, and future seeing dragon) crazy things happen. Turtle is also an animus so he made a stick that could hide his entire life from Darkstalker, which means he can't read his thoughts and he does not even know he exists, so he could spy on him. This book leaves many cliffhangers though which can be irritating at times and is sometimes hard to follow, but otherwise this is a very good book. I hope if you ever read it you will love is as much as I did. Now I am on book 10! I bet that one will be good too.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17912688198965821813">I didn't think I would be a fan of Turtle, but WOW WAS I WRONG.  We're talking about a dragon who suffers from extreme guilt and, possibly, anxiety.  Turtle spends the entire book berating himself for what he does, telling himself he's failing or a lesser dragon, so when his past issues were resolved and things said to him that relieved the guilt he carried for years, I wanted to scream and dance for him.  It was so wonderful.<br/><br/>The all-out animus battle between Turtle and someone else epic, and I </span>
  <span id="freeText17912688198965821813" style="display:none">I didn't think I would be a fan of Turtle, but WOW WAS I WRONG.  We're talking about a dragon who suffers from extreme guilt and, possibly, anxiety.  Turtle spends the entire book berating himself for what he does, telling himself he's failing or a lesser dragon, so when his past issues were resolved and things said to him that relieved the guilt he carried for years, I wanted to scream and dance for him.  It was so wonderful.<br /><br />The all-out animus battle between Turtle and someone else epic, and I loved seeing more of the animus magic and having it explained.  The animus magic is somewhat impossible to control, so it was interesting to have them fighting a villain where they couldn't use magic to throw some spears at him.  They had to be clever and very careful about what spells they used.  It made what could have been moments of "magicking" situations away to magic being either never used or used unexpectedly to continue Turtle's journey.<br /><br />Also I totally ship him and Kinkajou.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1867265596" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13157113597345283579">It's rare to find a book series that everyone in my family reads and enjoys (from 11yo to 43yo)! The stories are interesting and give us lots of references for discussion. In this particular book, we have already talked about making choices out of fear or out of conviction. This one was a bit slower than previous volumes-not much movement in the big story arc-but no less enjoyable. Sutherland is an excellent storyteller; we always feel transplanted into the story and reluctant to finish each boo</span>
  <span id="freeText13157113597345283579" style="display:none">It's rare to find a book series that everyone in my family reads and enjoys (from 11yo to 43yo)! The stories are interesting and give us lots of references for discussion. In this particular book, we have already talked about making choices out of fear or out of conviction. This one was a bit slower than previous volumes-not much movement in the big story arc-but no less enjoyable. Sutherland is an excellent storyteller; we always feel transplanted into the story and reluctant to finish each book.<br /><br />There's occasional violence, and an ongoing threat for humans, so if your preteens are extra-sensitive, this might not be a good choice. Parents should also know that some of the characters use magic...and not always for positive reasons. Otherwise, I/we HIGHLY recommend this book series to just about everyone we know!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13157113597345283579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1746390555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18131164114756335948">In the newest book in the WOF series, there was a lot of minute shifts and changes to the plotline. Overall, I loved this book. Tui never lets you down when it comes to WOF. There were so many things that you had to keep track of, and I'm gonna have to read it again. I like the style that she is going for: a story that keeps you guessing and on your toes, but still with the action/adventure elements involved. My favorite scene was when Turtle and Anemone were battling with their spells. It reall</span>
  <span id="freeText18131164114756335948" style="display:none">In the newest book in the WOF series, there was a lot of minute shifts and changes to the plotline. Overall, I loved this book. Tui never lets you down when it comes to WOF. There were so many things that you had to keep track of, and I'm gonna have to read it again. I like the style that she is going for: a story that keeps you guessing and on your toes, but still with the action/adventure elements involved. My favorite scene was when Turtle and Anemone were battling with their spells. It really shows just exactly what limits animus magic has. Which is absolutely NONE. The author likes to drop subtle hints in the text of the stories, like how the air buzzed and shocked them when they passed through the old Night Kingdom. I can't wait for the next book, because they never disappoint.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18131164114756335948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kB1vcAru5F7n+qD/vKfFGeqS5OUk8BqRXihkPACtOFhh7PL7wHrR/2uuEiCKXVcI7rnIQ8J7AWwk0bM18y/w2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wq06aFkEd46GyHLSHXHjHQMDAgr9aSvtiUV2M4KZN1qrXKfjk5BCLwqcwA0ri3EMBygurBviMBDzvKE6cRv/2w==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14193442424896408583">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br/><br/>Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br/><br/>I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay</span>
  <span id="freeText14193442424896408583" style="display:none">Okay, I know what you’re thinking. Tui? What kind of name is that? Is it short for something?<br /><br />Nope. Among the many great things to come out of New Zealand (the Lord of the Rings movies, cats that paint, my mom) is a bird called the tui—not as well known as the kiwi, but a heck of a lot noisier!<br /><br />I was born July 31 (same birthday as Harry Potter!) in Caracas, Venezuela, and lived in Asuncion, Paraguay; Miami, Florida; and Santo Domingo, Dominican Republic, before moving to New Jersey in high school, where I started doing theatre—mostly backstage work, because (a) it was fun, and (b) you got to hang out in the dark with cute boys. (Er, I mean . . . because it was artistically fulfilling, yes.)<br /><br />I graduated from Williams College in ’98 and I currently live in Boston with my husband, my perfect new baby, and my adorable yoodle Sunshine (what’s a yoodle? A puppy that’s three-quarters poodle and one-quarter Yorkshire terrier, of course!).<br /><br />Much to my parents’ relief, I abandoned my theatrical aspirations after college for the far more stable and lucrative career of fiction writing.<br /><br />My first two official books were beginning readers, part of Grosset &amp; Dunlap’s “First Friends” series for kids learning to read. MEET MO AND ELLA is tough to find now, but FUN WITH MO AND ELLA should still be out there somewhere.<br /><br />My first novel for teenagers was THIS MUST BE LOVE, which retells Shakespeare’s play A Midsummer Night’s Dream in a modern-day high school, from the POV of the two heroines, Hermia and Helena.<br /><br />And now I'm writing in a new project called SEEKERS! It's a children's book series that I'm writing with Erin Hunter. Check out my blog to find out more!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14193442424896408583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
